  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5171ac51-fea0-4bc1-b2d6-f025ff8f778c'

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/431966-can-anybody-say-what-this-book-is-about">Can anybody say what this book is about? The synopsis provided (on goodreads) really confused me, and although I am intrigued, I still feel like I don&#39;t know what the story is. Is this how I should go into the story, not knowing anything? Any more info out there?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_431966'><a id="like_count_community_question_431966" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/431966?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">8 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F18075234-challenger-deep">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/29448420-alex"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1449373021i/29448420._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/29448420-alex">Alex</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    This book is, essentially, about Caden's descent into mental illness. He has paranoia and delusions as well as full on hallucinations. We experience t<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    This book is, essentially, about Caden's descent into mental illness. He has paranoia and delusions as well as full on hallucinations. We experience the world through his mind and so see his hallucinations from his own perspective. It seems that there are two narratives, one that is "real" and one that is his delusions, but the two begin to overlap and merge in many ways. We follow Caden as his friends and family start to see there may be something wrong with Caden, through his admittance into a mental hospital and the things that he experiences there. The whole book is both real and surreal, so it is a little hard to describe.<br />I will say it takes a bit to get into, so keep reading even if you are confused. You're supposed to be a little confused. <br />Hope that helps!<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/43469491-kyla"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1471583655i/43469491._UY100_CR25,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/43469491-kyla">Kyla</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I found that the homeless guy with the Captain Crunch cereal box on his head whom Caden met when he was ten and gave chocolate coins to was the Captai<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I found that the homeless guy with the Captain Crunch cereal box on his head whom Caden met when he was ten and gave chocolate coins to was the Captain. As to why he's trying to lure Caden into the disease, I didn't see him as having his own kinds of goals and motivations like a normal fictional character because he was a figment of Caden's imagination whose purpose was to represent his illness. I would infer that the homeless guy with the Captain Crunch hat was the first person Caden ever met with a psychosis like his ended up being, and so he subconsciously chose that man to represent his descent into madness. As Caden wasn't aware of what was real and what was invented by his own mind, he did truly believe what the Captain told him, much like how we believe a dream is real while we're dreaming it, and only realise it isn't when we wake up (unless you've mastered lucid dreaming, of course).<br />Hope this helped!<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

<div id="review_1830531189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1830531189" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1830531189?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830531189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6937698039512594051">WOW I am blown away by this novel. This is an intense, intense story that you really need to dedicate yourself to reading. It is a truly incredible work of literature and absolutely deserves the title of National Book Award Winner. Eye-opening, thought-provoking, all around amazing.<br/><br/>TW: schizophrenia, talk of suicide<br/><br/>This is genuinely one of the greatest books I have ever read about mental illness. It is accurate, well-rounded, authentic as raw. As someone who suffered from a form of psychosis sim</span>
  <span id="freeText6937698039512594051" style="display:none">WOW I am blown away by this novel. This is an intense, intense story that you really need to dedicate yourself to reading. It is a truly incredible work of literature and absolutely deserves the title of National Book Award Winner. Eye-opening, thought-provoking, all around amazing.<br /><br />TW: schizophrenia, talk of suicide<br /><br />This is genuinely one of the greatest books I have ever read about mental illness. It is accurate, well-rounded, authentic as raw. As someone who suffered from a form of psychosis similar to schizophrenia, <i>Challenger Deep</i> was so validating to read. I honestly don’t know how Neal Schusterman captured <b>exactly</b> what this condition is like. Through collaborating with his son who deals with Caden’s illness and the immense amount of research put in, he somehow took the thoughts, feelings, and experiences that millions of people have and put it to paper. Color me entirely impressed by the fantastic portrayal of mental illness.<br /><br />I will say, <i>Challenger Deep</i> has an unconventional storytelling format. Half the story is told from Caden's perspective in his hometown and the other half is from Caden's perspective on a sailing ship. While I can attest to the many reviews suggesting this was confusing, I believe it is crucial to what makes <i>Challenger Deep</i> so unique and intense. I struggled a bit in the beginning as the two perspectives seem so disjointed but it quickly becomes easy to understand the intent behind these passages. <br /><br />Overall, <i>Challenger Deep</i> was amazing. I cannot recommend it enough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6937698039512594051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1155690938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1155690938" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1155690938?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061134111" href="/book/show/22864710-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=own-physical">own-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1155690938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6478288047275386537"><i>"Dead kids are put on pedestals, but mentally ill kids get hidden under the rug."</i><br/><br/>Thank you, Neal Shusterman, for portraying the pain, the horrors, and the light touches of hope that come with mental illness. I have read at least one book (looking at you, <i>All the Bright Places</i>) that glamorizes mental disorders, and as an aspiring psychologist, such inaccurate perceptions of these real diseases disturb me. Through Caden, Shusterman shows the delusions and doubts and episodes of emotional dysregula</span>
  <span id="freeText6478288047275386537" style="display:none"><i>"Dead kids are put on pedestals, but mentally ill kids get hidden under the rug."</i><br /><br />Thank you, Neal Shusterman, for portraying the pain, the horrors, and the light touches of hope that come with mental illness. I have read at least one book (looking at you, <i>All the Bright Places</i>) that glamorizes mental disorders, and as an aspiring psychologist, such inaccurate perceptions of these real diseases disturb me. Through Caden, Shusterman shows the delusions and doubts and episodes of emotional dysregulation that come with schizoaffective disorder, and he does so in a way that advances the plot while honoring the pain that pervades Caden's struggle.<br /><br />Despite my enjoyment of the book, I do wonder how younger readers with less knowledge about mental illnesses will perceive Shusterman's dual narratives. He switches between Caden's deterioration as he enters a mental institute and Caden's hallucinations of serving as a crewmate on a ship with a terrifying captain. I often felt a disconnect from Caden when he experienced his hallucinatory episodes (which makes sense, because of just how powerful and real they feel to him), and I question how other readers will construe Shusterman's narrative structure in <i>Challenger Deep</i>. Either way, he never makes light of Caden's situation or makes the mistake of glorifying it, which already sets this book apart from others.<br /><br />Overall, a gripping read and affecting novel about a boy torn between two realities. Recommended to those who enjoy contemporary YA, feel an interest about a book that centers on mental illness, and to fans of Shusterman's other works.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6478288047275386537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1083722838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083722838" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1083722838?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061134111" href="/book/show/22864710-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2015">best-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-without-romance">ya-without-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083722838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14209572517843241809"><b>This book is a blue puzzle pice of emotional genius.</b> I am affected. I AM VERY AFFECTED. At first I felt like I was sliding headfirst and upside down through a tunnel...the prose was so very <i>woah</i>. Like Alice in Wonderland but making LESS sense. I panicked for a moment that I wouldn't like this book, but come on! IT'S NEAL SHUSTERMAN. I trust him. And oh, gosh, it paid off. <b>This is the kind of story that gets lodged in your throat until you shout about it's marvellousness.</b> SO HERE I AM. SHOUTING. </span>
  <span id="freeText14209572517843241809" style="display:none"><b>This book is a blue puzzle pice of emotional genius.</b> I am affected. I AM VERY AFFECTED. At first I felt like I was sliding headfirst and upside down through a tunnel...the prose was so very <i>woah</i>. Like Alice in Wonderland but making LESS sense. I panicked for a moment that I wouldn't like this book, but come on! IT'S NEAL SHUSTERMAN. I trust him. And oh, gosh, it paid off. <b>This is the kind of story that gets lodged in your throat until you shout about it's marvellousness.</b> SO HERE I AM. SHOUTING. <br /><br /><b>It's about mental illness, yes.</b> But it's different. I recently read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23588512.Alice_and_the_Fly" title="Alice and the Fly by James Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Alice and the Fly</a> which also heavily featured schizophrenia. But the two are kind of incomparable. It has more of a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/248704.It_s_Kind_of_a_Funny_Story" title="It's Kind of a Funny Story by Ned Vizzini" rel="nofollow noopener">It's Kind of a Funny Story</a> vibe since the protagonist, Caden, is hospitalised during most of the book. I did appreciate that the book was about NOT putting on labels, and not squashing people into boxes. I want to <i>hug</i> it for that. Because THANK YOU. I wish more books had this kind of message. It took me on a very real roller coaster ride through medication and therapy and the pits of despair and recovery and the realisation that you <b>can't cure mental illness, but you can manage it.</b> Which is where I think a lot of books fail. BUT THIS ONE WINS THE WORLD.<br /><br /><blockquote> There are many things I don't understand, but here's one thing that I know: There is no such thing as a "correct" diagnosis. There are only symptoms and catchphrases for various collections of symptoms. </blockquote><br /><br /><b>This is a very personal book too, and I felt that while reading it.</b> Then I read the author's note. He quotes that 1 in 3 people suffer from mental illness, and most of the experiences in this book come from <i>his</i> own personal family life, particularly his son. His son did the artwork for the book. Imagine putting so MUCH of yourself and your family in a book?!! It's incredibly brave. And I think it makes a huge difference. <b>I just felt so connected to the book the whole time.</b> I haven't experienced the depths that CHALLENGER DEEP explores, but I do suffer with anxiety and, gah, this book summed up SO much stuff so completely well. IT'S LITERALLY EXTRAORDINARY.<br /><br /><b>Okay, so the book is written kind of oddly though...half is real life, half is imaginary.</b> I confess to being more interested in the real life parts. I guess it's a parellel. I struggled to match things up exactly...but I did see the comparisons! And that was incredible! I also love how, subtly, towards the end, the imaginary chapters were leaking into the real-life ones. It was so seamless and terrifying. <b>I had a rocky start with the beginning because NOTHING made sense.</b> But either I got used to it, or it smoothed out, but either way, the writing is flawless. It's delusional. It explains and makes you experience the fear and horror of being caught in delusions and <i>knowing</i> it's not real, but having to believe the delusions anyway. <br /><br /><b>Also, Caden's family just are great.</b> While Caden's losing himself in the delusions, they're <i>there</i> for him. CAN I JUST SAY, THANK YOU? It's so uplifting and hopeful. <br /><br /><b>I basically love this story.</b> It's scary and sad and confusing -- which exactly sums up what it's like to be mentally ill. It has PERFECT parallels. It explains things, and I think it'd make anyone empathises with the symptoms. It's loaded with extraordinary writing and a character my heart just broke for. This is easily an extraordinary book. <br /><br />HOLD ME, I'M HAVING TOO MANY EMOTIONS ABOUT THIS STORY. <br /><br />***<br /><br /><blockquote> The fear of not living is a deep, abiding dread of watching your own potential decompose into irredeemable disappointment when "should be" gets crushed by what is. Sometimes I think it would be easier to die than to face that, because "what could have been" is much more highly regarded than "what should have been". <i>Dead kids are put on pedestals, but mentally ill kids get hidden under the rug</i>.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>"At home they expect you to be fixed," she says. "They say they understand, but the only people who really understand are the ones who've been to That Place, too. It's like a man telling a woman he knows what it feels like to give birth." She turns to me, forsaking her view for a moment. "You will never know that, so don't pretend you do."</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="14209572517843241809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer687918517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5278166648160352242">UPDATE: Neal Shusterman has won the National Book Award for Young People’s Literature for this book! OHMYGOD!<br/><br/>EDIT: So this book is longlisted on National Book Awards. Yay!!! <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.newyorker.com/books/page-turner/the-national-book-awards-longlist-young-peoples-literature'>http://www.newyorker.com/books/page-t...</a><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"We are, however, creatures of containment. We want all things in life packed into boxes that we can label. But just because we have the ability to label it, doesn't mean we really know what's in the box. It's kind of like religion. It gives us comfort to believe we have defined som</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5278166648160352242" style="display:none">UPDATE: Neal Shusterman has won the National Book Award for Young People’s Literature for this book! OHMYGOD!<br /><br />EDIT: So this book is longlisted on National Book Awards. Yay!!! <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.newyorker.com/books/page-turner/the-national-book-awards-longlist-young-peoples-literature">http://www.newyorker.com/books/page-t...</a><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"We are, however, creatures of containment. We want all things in life packed into boxes that we can label. But just because we have the ability to label it, doesn't mean we really know what's in the box. It's kind of like religion. It gives us comfort to believe we have defined something that is, by its very nature, indefinable. As to whether or not we've gotten it right, well, it's all a matter of faith."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>This book is so deep I can see Adele rolling in it. </b> <br /><br />I know it's lame lol sorry. I sound like a 9gag commenter. Hahaha!<br /><br />Kidding aside, Challenger Deep is a precious, beautiful book about the reality of mental illness. Confusing at first yet compelling until the end, this book conveyed an important message to the readers regarding with that sensitive matter.<br /><br />I'm no expert but I think Neal Shusterman did a great job in depicting what is going on a mind of someone suffering from a mental illness. He masterfully crafted and told a story of a boy who's torn between the real and the imaginary without romanticizing it.<br /><br />Challenger Deep is subtle and poignant. And me reviewing this book is like a betrayal since I can't give justice of how important this book is. I hope you can read it, too.<br /><br />I really don't know what else to say but I think having a heartache and being teary-eyed while reading this book and typing this review will be enough to describe what I wanted to say.</span>

<div id="review_1294635250" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1294635250" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14811808-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585394064p2/14811808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1294635250?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/14811808-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=top-10-of-2015">top-10-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=worth-re-reading">worth-re-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1294635250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13395632230358446373">My first impression of this book was also the one that lasted - <i>While reading I often felt like I was drowning in it; and about as often like I was re-emerging.</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393021776ra/8649405.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I will try to write a review that does this magnificent book justice, but I am also fully aware of the fact that no matter what I say and how, I will not be able to encompass it all. <br/>But let's start at the beginning - Normally, I avoid books about mental illness as I avoid books about cancer. Authors often spiral out of control and go cra</span>
  <span id="freeText13395632230358446373" style="display:none">My first impression of this book was also the one that lasted - <i>While reading I often felt like I was drowning in it; and about as often like I was re-emerging.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393021776ra/8649405.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I will try to write a review that does this magnificent book justice, but I am also fully aware of the fact that no matter what I say and how, I will not be able to encompass it all. <br>But let's start at the beginning - Normally, I avoid books about mental illness as I avoid books about cancer. Authors often spiral out of control and go crashing into banalities and sugarcoating. <br>Not this book. <br><br>I picked it up because of the reference to the Mariana Trench, I wanted to know whether it would end at the title or whether the author would explore it further and draw more parallels. In order to avoid spoilers I will not answer the question - find it out yourself.<br>What I will say however is - nothing could have prepared me for <b>
  <u>this.</u>
</b><br>Imagine this -<i>you are underwater with your face turned towards the surface. Beneath you is the bottomless darkness and you know you are sinking, deeper and deeper, but you are not frightened. Instead you watch the sunrays dance on the surface, you watch the waves, you may even hear something happening above you though it is muted. Everything is muted. You are in some strange, undescribable vacuum or maybe limbo. You know you have to re-emerge soon, the sooner the better, but you are torn. A part of you wants to stay this way, the other desires to escape the water and never enter it again. Focus on what you are feeling, on what you are not feeling.</i><br>It is a strange state to be in, isn't it? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445121208ra/16602482.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>(I have no idea why, but this book reminded me of the atmosphere of 'Spirited Away' and especially No-Face. Maybe because both the mentioned character and this book had some unique imperturbability about them)</i><br><br>The author constantly switches between two settings, the reality and the delusion of Caden's life. Through the use of mostly brief and emotionally intense chapters the atmosphere changes rapidly leaving the reader more often than not somewhere between confused, shocked and heartbroken. There is certainly no action in this book - it is deeply introspective and psychological but not plot-driven. As I have already said, there is a calmness in it that is both stunning and scary. <br>It is very soon that the reader realises that it is about a scattered mind and follows Caden's journey, or rather journeys. Watches him losing himself to his delusions and getting more and more out of control until, finally, he is hospitalized. There are so many chapters that are entirely detached from reality and all of them are allegorical. In these chapters every phrase, every turn of the head, has a meaning and it is not always graspable, neither to the reader nor to Caden. Likewise, there are many chapters that are real and shocking, yet somewhat hopeful, because there are people in Caden's life who are willing to help him, who are there for him and support him during his difficult episodes. <br>The book is scary and confusing and moving and heartbreaking. And I loved every second of it and deeply appreciated the insight and the honesty behind it. Following the deterioration of Caden's sanity was both horrifying and enlightning and this is probably one of the very few books that will stay with me for a long, long time. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1437172473ra/15544991.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The author does not glamorize mental illness. Not even once - which makes it even more heart-wrenching. No one is put into boxes, there is no sugarcoating. There is however the truth, the way a person experienced mental illness first-hand. <br>This book carries an important, poignant message which is worth sharing and which should be spread. <u>
  <b>HIGHLY recommended.</b>
</u><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445119585ra/16602312.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>P.S. Only now, after going through the review to check for mistakes do I realise in what an emotional turmoil this book left me. I am still not over it. <br><br>P.P.S. <b>
  <i>READ IT.</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13395632230358446373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1455834849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455834849" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455834849?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061134142" href="/book/show/26073879-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455834849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14082558666531544750">I’m not sure what to rate this book.<br/>On one hand, there were so many moments where I had the overwhelming urge to cry, because the depiction of mental health in the story was so raw, brutally honest and to a certain extend, relatable. <br/><br/>On the other hand, I had quite a few moments where I couldn’t connect with the story and the overwhelming symbolism would throw me off. <br/><br/>It might have been better had I taken more time with it, since it required some effort on my part to fully grasp the meanings.<br/><br/>The </span>
  <span id="freeText14082558666531544750" style="display:none">I’m not sure what to rate this book.<br />On one hand, there were so many moments where I had the overwhelming urge to cry, because the depiction of mental health in the story was so raw, brutally honest and to a certain extend, relatable. <br /><br />On the other hand, I had quite a few moments where I couldn’t connect with the story and the overwhelming symbolism would throw me off. <br /><br />It might have been better had I taken more time with it, since it required some effort on my part to fully grasp the meanings.<br /><br />The story is powerful though and I do recommend it. It felt personal as some aspects were based on his son's experience with schizophrenia. The chapters are short and interchange between the present and diving into the mind of the character who suffers from schizophrenia and the world he has build for himself. Or more correctly, his delusions. And those two correlating viewpoints colliding.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14082558666531544750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1265683943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1265683943" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1265683943?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=amazing-writing">amazing-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=unreliable-narrator">unreliable-narrator</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=best-of-2015">best-of-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2015">arc-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=harper-teen">harper-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1265683943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10005832416082475673">This is the third gorgeously written book with positive representation of mental illness I’ve read this month. Third! It looks like YA is finally going there, endeavoring to explore the unexplorable. Neal Shusterman’s new book, Challenger Deep is the latest and brightest attempt to shed some light onto the struggles of people with mental disorders. <br/><br/>Challenger Deep is a magical book – smart and funny, intelligent and poignant, frightening and thought provoking – all at once. The mood changes with</span>
  <span id="freeText10005832416082475673" style="display:none">This is the third gorgeously written book with positive representation of mental illness I’ve read this month. Third! It looks like YA is finally going there, endeavoring to explore the unexplorable. Neal Shusterman’s new book, Challenger Deep is the latest and brightest attempt to shed some light onto the struggles of people with mental disorders. <br><br>Challenger Deep is a magical book – smart and funny, intelligent and poignant, frightening and thought provoking – all at once. The mood changes with each extremely brief chapter, and the rapid changes serve not only to manipulate our mood, but also to truly impress upon us that we’ve entered a scattered mind. This time, Shusterman writes from experience; his own son struggled with mental illness and the illustrations included in his book are Brendan’s from those times. <br><br>I suppose if you don’t know what to expect, Challenger Deep can be a bit tricky at first. Some chapters are accessible and realistic, and then there are those that are completely detached from reality. To add to that, the unrealistic chapters are deeply allegorical, and although it quickly becomes clear what they represent, getting to that point can be a bit trying. But everything you have to go through to fully experience this book is more than worth it. While it can be challenging at times, it’s also extremely rewarding. <br><br>The story has no less than three layers: the more or less healthy family life from Caiden’s memories, the rapid deterioration of his sanity and finally his life on the ship, an obvious metaphor and a sign of sanity lost. The whole decline is simply heartbreaking, but Shusterman still manages to make it all run smoothly. <br><br>Understanding mental illness and stopping discrimination against people who struggle with it is the next important step this society needs to take. Each decade has its own civil rights fight, and I truly hope we tackle this next. Books like Challenger Deep are extremely important in that regard and as someone whose family battled those same issues, I thank Neal and Brendan Shusterman from the bottom of my heart.<br><br>Every YA reader out there knows Neal Shusterman’s name, and if they don’t, I can honestly say they should. This is an author who constantly pushes the limits, who turns YA into something new and entirely unexpected each time. He should be celebrated far and wide and his work, more specifically this book, should get the accolades it deserves.<br><br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2391247026" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2391247026" />
    <a title="Fuzaila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55299343-fuzaila"><img alt="Fuzaila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532881347p2/55299343.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2391247026?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fuzaila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fuzaila" href="/user/show/55299343-fuzaila">Fuzaila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062231727" href="/book/show/22836584-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Fuzaila by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/52844833-laura-herondale">Laura Herondale</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=life-changing">life-changing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=favorite-dads">favorite-dads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=recommended-by-friends">recommended-by-friends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=why-no-hype">why-no-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=liked-it-but-i-am-not-sure">liked-it-but-i-am-not-sure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2391247026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1151126688023365014"><b>No combination of twenty-six letters can express what this book did to me.</b> <br/><br/> I’ve never been diagnosed with any kind of mental illness. I’ve had bad days - days when I felt like I was the only living being in the planet and everyone else was plotting against me. I’ve had suicidal thoughts for three days at a stretch. I secretly used to think that I might have survived depression once. Those thoughts feel laughable now. I thought I<i> knew</i> mental illness. I could usually <i>connect</i> with mentally ill cha</span>
  <span id="freeText1151126688023365014" style="display:none"><b>No combination of twenty-six letters can express what this book did to me.</b> <br /><br /> I’ve never been diagnosed with any kind of mental illness. I’ve had bad days - days when I felt like I was the only living being in the planet and everyone else was plotting against me. I’ve had suicidal thoughts for three days at a stretch. I secretly used to think that I might have survived depression once. Those thoughts feel laughable now. I thought I<i> knew</i> mental illness. I could usually <i>connect</i> with mentally ill characters in books and I used to think I <i>knew </i>what it felt like. APPARENTLY NOT.<br /><br /><u> This book just changed my life.</u> <br /><br />Shusterman’s story is brilliantly crafted, original, and well researched and the artworks are <b>
  <i>real</i>
</b>. It is an exemplar for mental illness books. He has captured so well what it is like to be mentally ill, drawing from his own experiences as well as his son's, who had been schizophrenic. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “I push through the granite, the sludge, the bones, the dirt, the worms, and the termites, until I’m bursting through into some rice paddy field in China, proving that there’s no such thing as down, because eventually down is up.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /> Honestly, why isn’t anyone reading this instead of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28954189.Scythe__Arc_of_a_Scythe___1_" title="Scythe (Arc of a Scythe, #1) by Neal Shusterman" rel="nofollow noopener">Scythe</a>? Like, <b>this is IMPORTANT. This is EXTRAORDINARY. This is a MUST READ</b>.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “It’s not like I can control these feelings. It’s not like I mean to think these thoughts. They’re just there, unwanted birthday gifts that you can’t give back.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Caden Bosch</b> is fifteen. He is schizophrenic and maybe schizoaffective. He is in a ship that sails to nowhere. He also goes to school and has two best friends who have been recently thrown off by his strange behavior. He’s in search of the depth of Marianas Trench in the Pacific Ocean. He can see things others can’t. He knows what people are thinking when they don’t know themselves. He knows truth about this universe no one has yet discovered. <b>He is mentally ill.</b> And this, is his story. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “Do you know how it feels, to be free from yourself and terrified by it? You feel both invincible and targeted, as if the world – as if the universe – doesn’t want you to feel this dizzying enlightenment. And you know there are forces out there that want to crush your spirit like a gas filling all available space. Now the voices are loud, almost as loud as your mother as she calls you down for dinner for the third time. You know it’s the third time even though you don’t remember hearing the first two times. Even though you don’t even remember going up to your room.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b> <br /> <br />This book did to me what no other book has. I can’t really explain. I had an intense head-ache while reading it. I began to see things that weren’t there. The only time I had hallucinations was this one time when I was fifteen and sick. I’d stayed awake all night staring at the dark ceiling, feeling that the ceiling fan was dropping monsters at me, the room was trying to shrink into me, that I was falling into an abyss I couldn’t escape from. I might have puked a few times that night. <u>I can’t begin to imagine what it would be like to live like that <b><i>all the time</i></b></u>. I experienced it now. <b>I deeply resonated with Caden Bosch and his thoughts. </b>I had to stop reading at times, scared to continue, thinking that maybe I’m becoming schizophrenic myself. I felt like I was floating an inch from the ground, like I had lost all purpose. I honestly couldn’t sleep well at all.<b> That is how deep and intensely vivid Shusterman’s writing is.</b> It speaks directly to your brain. <b>It consumes you in whole</b>.<br /><br />That was mostly for the first half of the book. The second half sometimes felt dragged on. I particularly didn’t enjoy the ship scenes much. Mostly because I was confused on what was going on. <br /><br /><b>But then, it becomes all too clear.</b><br /><br />I teared up at times. <br /><br />I related to Caden. <br /><br />I became scared. <br /><br />I worried.<br /><br /><b>I even thought of DNFing the book just to end turmoil it was putting me through.</b> <br /><br /><u>But in the end, I just marveled at how deeply and intensely this book affected me. </u><br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “And that knowledge is so magnificent you can’t hold it in, and it drives you to share it – but you don’t have the words to describe it, and without the words, without a way to share the feeling, it breaks you, because your mind just isn’t large enough to hold what you’ve tried to fit into it…”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br />Please people, <b>GO AND READ THIS BOOK. </b>It is going to change your perspective on life, and you’ll never read a mental-illness rep the same way ever again. Not that I wish anyone to go through what I did while reading it, but I want everybody to read this book and have their eyes open.<br /><br />°•°•°•°•°•°•°•°•°•°•°•°•°•°•°•°<br /><br /><b>I’m deeply grateful to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52844833" rel="nofollow noopener">Laura</a> for recommending me this book. I know I wouldn’t have discovered this otherwise. Thanks lovely! xD</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1151126688023365014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1665112814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1665112814" />
    <a title="Brian Yahn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22849115-brian-yahn"><img alt="Brian Yahn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464719293p2/22849115.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1665112814?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian Yahn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian Yahn" href="/user/show/22849115-brian-yahn">Brian Yahn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1665112814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3325075635082653546">Neal Shusterman writes like he’s a wizard and Challenger Deep is his spellbook. The prose is enthralling, think Truman Capote meets Junot Diaz--world class stuff here, honestly.<br/><br/>He puts you through a child’s mental illness by taking you on a voyage across the sea, on a pirate sheep, to the depths of Challenger Deep. The mysterious way Caden ends up on this ship, and how strange the inhabitants are give the book a nonsensical feel, like Alice’s Adventures in Wonderland, but with a twist of mystery</span>
  <span id="freeText3325075635082653546" style="display:none">Neal Shusterman writes like he’s a wizard and Challenger Deep is his spellbook. The prose is enthralling, think Truman Capote meets Junot Diaz--world class stuff here, honestly.<br /><br />He puts you through a child’s mental illness by taking you on a voyage across the sea, on a pirate sheep, to the depths of Challenger Deep. The mysterious way Caden ends up on this ship, and how strange the inhabitants are give the book a nonsensical feel, like Alice’s Adventures in Wonderland, but with a twist of mystery that just keeps you DYING to learn more.<br /><br />The story unfolds in these very short, vignette-y scenes that are almost poetic. But like poetry, and maybe as the name implies, it’s quite the challenging read. The story unfolds in a way that feels as insane as the narrator. And at the end, it never quite fits together, like the metaphorical puzzle Caden and his friends never finish.<br /><br />Regardless, there’s something magical about this book. The pirate ship was the most interesting thing I’ve read in a long time, and even though I wish the whole book was about that journey and had nothing to do with mental illness, Neal Shusterman really blew me away with the book as a whole. Very satisfying, unique read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3325075635082653546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2291111928" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2291111928" />
    <a title="Iryna *Book and Sword*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword"><img alt="Iryna *Book and Sword*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547595130p2/57236678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2291111928?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Iryna *Book and Sword*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Iryna *Book and Sword*" href="/user/show/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword">Iryna *Book and Sword*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57236678-iryna-book-and-sword?shelf=from-the-library">from-the-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2291111928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5124058261920939341"><b>3.5/5 stars</b> <br/>(Goodreads please give us <b>half stars</b> soon please, and thank you!)<br/><br/>​<b>“I used to be afraid of dying. Now I’m afraid of not living. There’s a difference. We go through life planning for a future, but sometimes that future never comes.”</b><br/><br/>This was one of the hardest books I've ever read. I spent about three weeks on it, because I had to keep putting it down - the emotions of this book kept drowning me. I will be honest - if I didn't read other, more light hearted books while I was also readin</span>
  <span id="freeText5124058261920939341" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5 stars</b> <br />(Goodreads please give us <b>half stars</b> soon please, and thank you!)<br /><br />​<b>“I used to be afraid of dying. Now I’m afraid of not living. There’s a difference. We go through life planning for a future, but sometimes that future never comes.”</b><br /><br />This was one of the hardest books I've ever read. I spent about three weeks on it, because I had to keep putting it down - the emotions of this book kept drowning me. I will be honest - if I didn't read other, more light hearted books while I was also reading this, I'd be plunged into the pits of the deepest depression by now. <br /><br /><b>"Schizophrenia, schizoaffective, bipolar I, bipolar II, major depression, psychotic depression, obsessive/compulsive, and on, and on. The labels mean nothing, because no two cases are ever exactly alike. Everyone presents differently, and responds to meds differently, and no prognosis can truly be predicted." </b><br /><br />The premise of the book, the idea and the message were fantastic. I also really recommend reading the footnote by the author, Neil Shusterman, as he explains how the topic of his book and his family are intimately related. That brought a whole new level of depth to the book. <br /><br />So why only 3.5 stars? The book was great - there were so many amazing and quotable moments, if this wasn't a library copy, I'd have been highlighting the crap out of it. But where it was full of emotions it lacked in plot (for me at least). I found myself losing attention at the metaphoric parts and wanting to get to the real life parts. Later on in the book they merge and connect, but prior to that I have to admit, it was a bit confusing.<br /><br /><b>“You see demons in the eyes of the world, and the world sees a bottomless pit in yours.”</b><br /><br />The book also deals with prejudice and wrong accusations. How people see somebody who is different and immediately assume that person is a drug addict. And when they realize what's happening it is often way too late. <br /><br />​I believe that this book will help many people - it will show them that they are not alone, that no matter what they might be feeling, no matter how ludicrous it may be, there is somebody out there who had felt the same way, or still is.<br /><br />But I also believe that this book might trigger many others. The emotions in the book were so real you can feel them dripping off the pages. Caden's fears and his paranoia are contagious, and if you are not careful enough it will get you. It didn't help that I am already a hypochondriac and an ocd (self diagnosed, of course, but these things you just know). I kept thinking - am I going to spiral down one day? I have some symptoms, so is it a challenger deep for me too? <br /><br />Nobody ever likes to feel powerless, but when I read Challenger Deep I felt it - inability to help Caden, or others like Caiden - because only they can help themselves. Sure, doctors and nurses and medicine stabilize people, but in the end the journey is only that person's to take. <br /><br />Challenger Deep also gave me a new perspective on brain altering medicine. I still don't exactly know how I feel about it, but I do realize now that sometimes that is all doctors have - their best is just a guess, and sometimes that guess works and sometimes it doesn't. <br /><br /><b>“The fear of not living is a deep, abiding dread of watching your own potential decompose into irredeemable disappointment when 'should be' gets crushed by what is. Sometimes I think it would be easier to die than to face that, because 'what could have been' is much more highly regarded than 'what should have been.' Dead kids are put on pedestals, but mentally ill kids get hidden under the rug.”</b><br /><br />​I'd definitely recommend this book, but I will also say - be ready, this is not the easiest journey you will ever read through. And it will stay with you forever.<br /><br />My <a href="http://bookandsword.net " rel="nofollow noopener">WEBSITE</a><br />My <a href="https://www.instagram.com/book_and_sword/" rel="nofollow noopener">INSTAGRAM</a><br />My <a href="https://bookandswordblog.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">WORDPRESS BLOG</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5124058261920939341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2552311515" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2552311515" />
    <a title="Laysee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4863523-laysee"><img alt="Laysee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459741824p2/4863523.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2552311515?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laysee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laysee" href="/user/show/4863523-laysee">Laysee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Laysee by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4863038-winston">Winston</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2552311515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5115033805508187104"><b>Challenger Deep</b> is a brilliant and imaginative account of an adolescent’s descent into mental illness and his recovery. The author takes us into the disturbed mind of 15-year-old Caden Bosch and we perceive what it means to live in a world where reality keeps shifting and there is no true North. Caden is distracted by things he cannot see but can feel, such as termites he claims he can hear. I steeled myself for a difficult read, and it was difficult and longer than I liked it to be, but what I </span>
  <span id="freeText5115033805508187104" style="display:none"><b>Challenger Deep</b> is a brilliant and imaginative account of an adolescent’s descent into mental illness and his recovery. The author takes us into the disturbed mind of 15-year-old Caden Bosch and we perceive what it means to live in a world where reality keeps shifting and there is no true North. Caden is distracted by things he cannot see but can feel, such as termites he claims he can hear. I steeled myself for a difficult read, and it was difficult and longer than I liked it to be, but what I did not expect was to be entertained by the humor and zaniness that bubble up from a hidden place left seemingly intact within this battered youth. <br /><br />Having schizophrenia is likened to being on a pirate ship with a one-eyed captain wearing an eye patch and a one-eyed parrot also wearing an eye patch and an additional safety badge. On board ship is the crow’s nest where crewmen like Caden go to get their colorful cocktail a few times a day. Except that Caden’s drink glows like a lava lamp and is concocted from cartilage of cow and spine of black beetle! Caden is on a mission to the Challenger Deep, the deepest point on Earth, the southern icy end of the Marianas Trench.<br /><br />The captain is a mocking tyrant, regards Caden as a ‘malnourished pup’, and cuts off the limbs of crewmen who displease him. Caden is a budding artist but the captain informs him that he has no permission to have a talent. The parrot is no better; he is malevolent, too, but funny. The captain and the parrot behave like rivals in competition for Caden’s loyalty. It is hard to know if they are on Caden's side. There are some laughable interactions on board ship, which takes the weight off a book whose subject matter concerns the dark corners of the human mind. <br /><br />Caden is disturbed but has good insight when the oompah-loompas bouncing around his brain subside. On blue sky days, he recognizes he has more caring parents than his roommate. He feels his parents’ helplessness in their quest to save him. <i>‘The two of them are in a lifeboat, together, but so alone. Miles from shore, yet miles from me. The boat leaks, and they must bail in tandem to keep themselves afloat. It must be exhausting.’ </i>He can be unkindly honest and straight-talking during group therapy when participants are unhelpfully going in circles of revisiting past abuse week after week. Shusterman created a young hero we want to root for.<br /><br />Structurally, the chapters are very short and alternate between Caden on the pirate ship and Caden in a juvenile psychiatric ward. Interspersed between the chapters are the sketches and art work of a troubled soul. One of the first signs of hope is when the captain says to Caden, <i>‘This ship is more alive than you think, boy. She feels pain. She can be hurt but can also heal.’ </i>And Caden does heal over time.<br /><br /><b>Challenger Deep</b> is an ingenious way of illustrating the trials faced by individuals seeking help in a mental health care facility. It also subtly but respectfully reveals the limitations of antipsychotic medication and the delicacy of the group psychotherapy process.<br /><br />I was moved to learn that <b>Challenger Deep</b> is borne of Neal Shusterman’s own experience of having journeyed with his son who suffered a mental disorder. The art work in the book were drawn by his son when he was ill. That this book is not fiction lends it an authentic and powerful voice. It is the well-deserved recipient of the 2015 National Book Award for Young People’s Literature. This sensitive and sympathetic insider story of a fragmented mind that can become whole again is highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5115033805508187104" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1096018343?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Elizabeth" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth">Sarah Elizabeth</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1096018343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12168745008590379118">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to HarperCollins and Edelweiss.)<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Count your blessings,” the captain says, “And if you count less than ten, cut off the remaining fingers.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426944363i/14128730.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This story was just plain weird, and while I figured out after a while that it was actually about mental illness, it was still pretty weird.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Where does this hallway go?”<br/>She looks at me with suspicion. “It doesn’t go anywhere, it stays right here.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426944363i/14128731.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Caden was a boy </span>
  <span id="freeText12168745008590379118" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to HarperCollins and Edelweiss.)<br><br><b>
  <i>“Count your blessings,” the captain says, “And if you count less than ten, cut off the remaining fingers.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426944363i/14128730.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This story was just plain weird, and while I figured out after a while that it was actually about mental illness, it was still pretty weird.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Where does this hallway go?”<br>She looks at me with suspicion. “It doesn’t go anywhere, it stays right here.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426944363i/14128731.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Caden was a boy who had obviously got problems, the hallucinations that the was experiencing were so vivid that he actually believed that they were really happening to him, and his delusions about a boy at school who he had never spoken to wanting to kill him, did come across as a symptom of possible schizophrenia.<br><br><b>
  <i>“well, it’s just that… there’s this kid at school.”<br>“Yes?”<br>“Of course I can’t be sure…”<br>“Yes?”<br>“Well… I think he wants to kill me.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426944363i/14128732.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline in this was split in two, half of the time we were following Caden as he lived on a ship (which was very strange), and the other half of the time we saw Caden at home with his family, and experienced the strange ideas he came out with, and his admission to a mental health care facility. This was all a bit confusing though, and after a while I started to get a bit sick of the repetativeness of the story.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Cartilage of cow,” he tells, “and spine of black beetle.”<br>“Beetles have no spines,” I point out. “They’re invertebrates.”<br>“Exactly. That’s why it’s so rare.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426944363i/14128733._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending to this was okay, and I appreciated what the author had tried to do with this story, I just struggled to really enjoy this though.<br>6 out of 10<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12168745008590379118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1446455403" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1446455403" />
    <a title="Liz Janet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5114433-liz-janet"><img alt="Liz Janet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574021381p2/5114433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1446455403?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Janet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Janet" href="/user/show/5114433-liz-janet">Liz Janet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062413093" href="/book/show/24331542-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1446455403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18214102475351273519"><i>“And you know the darkness beyond despair, just as intimately as you know the soaring heights. Because in this and all universes, there is balance. You can't have the one without facing the other. And sometimes you think you can take it because the joy is worth the despair, and sometimes you know you can't take it and how did you ever think you could?”</i><br/><br/>This review will be filled with quotes, because almost everything in this book was quote-worthy. That is how beautiful it is. I will gush about it</span>
  <span id="freeText18214102475351273519" style="display:none"><i>“And you know the darkness beyond despair, just as intimately as you know the soaring heights. Because in this and all universes, there is balance. You can't have the one without facing the other. And sometimes you think you can take it because the joy is worth the despair, and sometimes you know you can't take it and how did you ever think you could?”</i><br /><br />This review will be filled with quotes, because almost everything in this book was quote-worthy. That is how beautiful it is. I will gush about it constantly, this book feels at par with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484935560?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">We Are The Ants</a> , and I loved that one. It will be one that keeps coming to mind over and over again.<br /><br />This is one of the few stories I've read, were the portrayal of mental illness is done so brilliantly that I can find no fault. It shows that although mental illness cannot be cured, it can be managed. This is the story of a boy's descent into schizophrenia, and his dabbles between the reality of it all, and the muddled allegories presented to him during his medicine and "bouts of insanity." <br /><br /> <b>
  <i>“And when the abyss looks into you - and it will - may you look back unflinching.”</i>
</b><br /><br />When I read this quote, I knew that the connection that I barely need or seek from a book had been achieved. It felt like an inspiration had been given to me, to stare back at the monster that may haunt my nightmares, and be not afraid. And for this, I could do nothing but recommend it to as many people as I can. People that duffer from mental illnesses are often told that they are weak for being ill, that it is their fault they are the way they are, that no one will ever love them because they cannot love themselves, this quote feels strong enough to give people the valor to start digging themselves out of the whole that varied and differing reasons have dug for them. At least as much as I've read in Young-Adult literature. <br /><br /><i>“I used to be afraid of dying. Now I’m afraid of not living. There’s a difference. </i><b>
  <i> We go through life planning for a future, but sometimes that future never comes.” </i>
</b> and <i>“Seeing monsters everywhere and realizing </i><b>
  <i>there aren't enough slingshots in the world to get rid of them.”</i>
</b><br /><br />One of the strongest things, which I had issues with in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/816417019?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Thirteen Reasons Why</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1526886965?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Bright Places</a>, was that mental illness is not romanticized. This story tells it like it is, without presuming that as soon as someone finds love, their illness will be cured, or how their disorder makes them all quirky and adorable, or how a suicide is the pinnacle of leaving earth. I like that, it makes it real, it is not eliminating the struggles which people have to endure in order to provide romance to a targeted audience. (notice that these books are targeted at teens that suffer the illnesses, but they are usually misrepresented, and their illness becomes the plot around romance)<br /><br /><i>“The fear of not living is a deep, abiding dread of watching your own potential decompose into irredeemable disappointment when 'should be' gets crushed by what is. Sometimes I think it would be easier to die than to face that, because 'what could have been' is much more highly regarded than 'what should have been.' </i><b>
  <i>Dead kids are put on pedestals, but mentally ill kids get hidden under the rug.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I live in America, and in this country, mental illness is not treated as the serious issue that deserves better medical coverage. And I know that is a gross generalization by saying that our mass-school shootings speak for themselves when it comes to this subject, but it is an affront to human decency to not provide any help for people that have a mental illness. Our media also has a big part in wrongly portraying it, mostly using it to present misguided and stereotypical views, which affects the culture, and how everyday people see it. I had a person once tell me that depression was just someone feeling down for a bit, and all they need to do is find a partner and that then they would be fine. I never stayed close to that person again to hear such idiocy come out of their mouth.<br /><br />There is also the very issue that if someone commits suicide, they are put in a pedestal, they are shown as tragic heroes, they are shown as spokespersons for anti-bulling campaigns, and although I see why it is important to highlight how bullying is a huge issue within our community, they also suffered the after effects of it via a mental illness. But no one talks about it, they choose to ignore it, in the hopes that if no one mentions it, it will go away. But it never does. <br /><br /><i>“We always look for the signs we missed when something goes wrong. We become like detectives trying to solve a murder, because maybe if we uncover the clues, it gives us some control. Sure, we can’t change what happened, but if we can string together enough clues, we can prove that whatever nightmare has befallen us, we could have stopped it, if only we had been smart enough.</i><b>
  <i>I suppose it’s better to believe in our own stupidity than it is to believe that all the clues in the world wouldn’t have changed a thing.”</i>
</b><br /><br />All I have to say is thank you Neal Shusterman, this book gave the emotional ride that few books have ever done. This is one I will read and read over and over, until I am probably dead. <br /><br /><i>“To name her is to sink her,” he told me. “That which we name takes greater weight than the sea it displaces. Ask any shipwreck.”“I know exactly what he means. I had overheard Poirot talking to my parents. He was using words like "psychosis" and "schizophrenic". Words that people feel they have to whisper, or not repeat at all. </i><b>
  <i>The Mental-Illness-That-Must-Not-Be-Named.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Once you make a Harry Potter reference that stands on its own, you've got me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18214102475351273519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1177518441" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1177518441" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1177518441?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alahna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alahna" href="/user/show/6916629-alahna">Alahna</a>
