        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6916629-alahna?shelf=realistic-ish-fiction">realistic-ish-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1177518441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5126021899001908925">This is probably one of the most manipulative books I've ever read. Not on purpose or anything, but I just feel like if I don't rate it high it means that don't care about people with mental illness and their struggles. But I think I am going to go ahead and give it 2 stars because I, myself, did not particularly enjoy reading this. This is definitely an important book and one of the best portrayals of mental illness i have ever read and I would TOTALLY recommend it to anyone who wanted to read </span>
  <span id="freeText5126021899001908925" style="display:none">This is probably one of the most manipulative books I've ever read. Not on purpose or anything, but I just feel like if I don't rate it high it means that don't care about people with mental illness and their struggles. But I think I am going to go ahead and give it 2 stars because I, myself, did not particularly enjoy reading this. This is definitely an important book and one of the best portrayals of mental illness i have ever read and I would TOTALLY recommend it to anyone who wanted to read about mental illness in YA. I was just bored the majority of the time. I think it was beautifully written, but it just wasn't really for me. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1890476449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1890476449" />
    <a title="Puck" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18562856-puck"><img alt="Puck" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498403772p2/18562856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1890476449?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Puck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Puck" href="/user/show/18562856-puck">Puck</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061134111" href="/book/show/22864710-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=favorites-2017">favorites-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18562856-puck?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1890476449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5013322688421328485"><i>
  <b> "Dead kids are put on pedestals, but mentally ill kids get hidden under the rug.” </b>
</i><br/><br/>This book is incredible. It’s the brave and harrowing, but above all brutally honest story of what it feels like to suffer from schizophrenia. Alongside Caden we confront it all: the delusions, the mania, the constant fear and doubts - but also the lights on the horizon and the support from friends and family. <b>Challenger Deep</b> is based on the experience of Shusterman’s best friend and own son with this mental i</span>
  <span id="freeText5013322688421328485" style="display:none"><i>
  <b> "Dead kids are put on pedestals, but mentally ill kids get hidden under the rug.” </b>
</i><br /><br />This book is incredible. It’s the brave and harrowing, but above all brutally honest story of what it feels like to suffer from schizophrenia. Alongside Caden we confront it all: the delusions, the mania, the constant fear and doubts - but also the lights on the horizon and the support from friends and family. <b>Challenger Deep</b> is based on the experience of Shusterman’s best friend and own son with this mental illness, which made this story all the more powerful. <br /><br />In this book we follow Caden Bosch, a 15-year-old teenage boy who's mind slowly gets taking over by terrifying hallucinations and intrusive thoughts. It starts out very small – him thinking there are termites living in the walls of his home – but when Caden starts to roam the streets in fear of /a boy he suspects is going to kill him/earthquakes/painted dolphins/<b>SOMETHING!</b>/ his parents admit him to a mental hospital.<br />In there Caden spends his time with group therapy sessions, medication cocktails, and talks with his psychiatrist. In his mind however, Caden is part of a ship’s crew, lead by a terrifying captain in search of Challenger Deep, an oceanic trench where the darkest monsters of all reside. <br /><br />Reading this book was a challenge, in more ways than one. A lot of chapters namely are about how Caden is trapped in the delusions of his own mind, where things from reality and his imagination come together on the ship. First I didn’t understand the chapters on the ship at all, but after 1/3 of the book things <i>click</i> and will start making sense. <br />The chapters spend in reality are more clear, but maybe more painful to read because the reader, alongside Caden, experiences the fear and anxiety while he slowly loses control of his own mind. The boy realises that his fears aren’t real, but he can’t help it: he HAS to run from the things that are chasing him. <br /><br /><i>“Don Quixote - the famous literary madman - fought windmills. People think he saw giants when he looked at them, but those of us who've been there know the truth. He saw windmills, just like everyone else - but he </i>believed<i> they were giants. The scariest thing of all is never knowing what you're suddenly going to believe.” </i><br /><br />This book offers a very positive and realistic view on medication and mental health clinics. In many (mental-health) books mental hospitals are demonized and described as prisons and mental torture houses run by cruel doctors and orderlies. This is <b>incredibly</b> damaging and harmful for the image of mental health as a whole, because in most cases (let’s be realistic), hospitals aren’t like that at all. Shusterman actively shows you how the medication and therapy sessions work by making the writing and the story more coherent the longer Caden stays in the clinic. Slowly you figure out who the ship’s crewmembers are, and whose words you can trust.<br /><br />But meds don’t make an illness disappear. A girl in the clinic comments that <i>“at home they all think medicine should be magic, and they become mad at me when it’s not.”</i> Not all the children in the clinic improve while they are there. A mental disorder, wherever it’s schizophrenia, depression, or OCD, can’t be cured: it’s something that you have to fight again and again and again. This struggle is incredibly difficult, but seeing how all the kids fight their inner demons with the support of each other, the doctors, and their family, is heart wrenching but very powerful. <br /><br />In the author’s note, Shusterman tells that “he hopes that this book will comfort those who have been there, letting them know they are not alone. We also hope that it will help others empathize, and to understand what it’s like to sail the dark, unpredictable waters of mental illness.” The aim of this book isn’t therefore only to entertain, but also to educate and make us aware of how mental illness can affect someone's life and the lives of others. <br />I’m very happy that I’ve read this book and will recommend it to anyone who is interested in reading books about mental health wherein nothing gets glamorized, or those who want to read an impactful story. Because this certainly made an impact on me. <br /><br /><br /><br /><i>This is the third book that I read for the <a href="https://mobile.twitter.com/diverseathon" rel="nofollow noopener">#DiverseAThon</a>, which ran from the 22nd to the 29th of January 2017.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5013322688421328485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2012791926" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2012791926" />
    <a title="Chance Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2355889-chance-lee"><img alt="Chance Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551884443p2/2355889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2012791926?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chance Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chance Lee" href="/user/show/2355889-chance-lee">Chance Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061134111" href="/book/show/22864710-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2355889-chance-lee?shelf=national-book-award">national-book-award</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2355889-chance-lee?shelf=j-fic">j-fic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2355889-chance-lee?shelf=no">no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2355889-chance-lee?shelf=blurb-d">blurb-d</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2012791926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5652877865931021379">I recently asked someone, "Would you rather travel into outer space or the deepest depths of the ocean?" He said, "There's nothing underwater. Outer space, there's so much out there." Yeah, if you're interested in flying rocks! My answer: The depths of the ocean, because there's so much fascinating life down where the sun cannot reach. But both would be too scary for me to actually attempt, because your vessel of choice could depressurize and turn your head inside out.<br/><br/>Shortly after that thought </span>
  <span id="freeText5652877865931021379" style="display:none">I recently asked someone, "Would you rather travel into outer space or the deepest depths of the ocean?" He said, "There's nothing underwater. Outer space, there's so much out there." Yeah, if you're interested in flying rocks! My answer: The depths of the ocean, because there's so much fascinating life down where the sun cannot reach. But both would be too scary for me to actually attempt, because your vessel of choice could depressurize and turn your head inside out.<br /><br />Shortly after that thought experiment, I read the blurb for this book: "Caden Bosch is on a ship that's headed for the deepest point on Earth: Challenger Deep, the southern part of the Marianas Trench."<br /><br />Serendipity! I immediately put in an ILL at my library.<br /><br />I should have kept reading, or, if I did, actually paid attention to what I read. The blurb continues, "Caden Bosch is a brilliant high school student whose friends are starting to notice his odd behavior." Okay, this is a kids' book. He could be on a ship <i>and</i> in school. That type of things happens in fiction. (In <i>bad</i> fiction!, I'd have said if I were paying attention.)<br /><br />The blurb continues, "Caden Bosch is designated the ship's artist in residence, to document the journey with images." Okay, this could be interesting, I'd think. <br /><br />Furthermore, "Caden Bosch pretends to join the school track team but spends his days walking for miles, absorbed by the thoughts in his head." Uhh, I guess you gotta keep moving when you're underwater. You wouldn't want all the fluid going to your legs or something, right? <br /><br />Finally, "Caden Bosch is split between his allegiance to the captain and the allure of mutiny." Ooh, drama! (Also, I hate when blurbs repeatedly name the character like I'm going to start chanting it as if he's my cult leader.)<br /><br />The way this blurb is written, I expected something akin to <i>The Abyss</i>. Deep sea exploration breeds paranoia and insecurity. Unfortunately, it's the opposite. Normal high school kid is grappling with schizophrenia. He hallucinates being on a weird ship, which only increases his all-too-real sense of paranoia. <br /><br />This story could be fascinating if written differently. There is no consistent structure. Chapters are very short, one- or two-pages long. The first five chapters are either dream sequences, rambling thoughts, or set on the ship. The next two chapters are in the character's reality, where he interacts with his mom and dad, his sister, and feels disconnected from his friends at school. Chapters 9-11 are set in the ship. 12-13 are reality. 14-17: ship. 18-19: reality. 20-21: ship. 22-24: reality? The chapters are sometimes punctuated by illustrations only a dad could love (the illustrator is Shusterman's son, and Shusterman says about his son's doodles, "There is no greater artwork in the world.")<br /><br />There is no rhythm to the chapter structure. I feel like the intent is to create "instability" in the narrative. "Being schizophrenic <i>is</i> confusing!" someone might say to justify this lack of structure, but it feels like Shusterman is using the inherent instability of mental illness as an excuse to not give his book a coherent rhythm or structure. Plus, the ship sequences are absurd. There's a magic talking parrot; the captain speaks in riddles; the crow's nest is bigger on the inside than the outside... and for what purpose? "It's an allegory!" someone might say to justify the incoherent contents of these chapters, but as a reader, I don't need 200 pages of allegory, and "allegory" isn't an excuse to throw stream-of-consciousness writing on the page and call it a novel. <br /><br />I started skipping the ship chapters and reading only the reality chapters. I didn't feel lost as a reader at all, but I did feel bored. I didn't find the writing particularly compelling. One entire chapter where the narrator morosely ponders the meaning of the phrase "a penny for your thoughts" grated on me. "If pennies become worthless, does that devalue our thoughts to less than nothing?" Ugh. <br /><br />I read the last few chapters to confirm that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[all the ship sequences are a product of the main character's mental illness. They are. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> If this book were about half the length, I may have gone on this journey into the depths. But, kind of like a twisted combination of my initial question that caused my attraction to this book, I've dove into the water and found only rocks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5652877865931021379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11774429762595365146"><b>Thank you Edelweiss and HarperCollins for providing me with an ARC of this book!</b><br/><br/><b><u>Short review</u>:</b> <br/><br/>I'm having a bit of difficulty expressing how I feel about this book. I really enjoyed it, and it had a lot of powerful moments. I appreciate that Neal Shusterman tackled a personal subject (from what I understand, his son struggles with mental illness––and actually did the illustrations in the book, which is cool).<br/><br/>To be honest, though, this was not my favorite of his books. While I think it's great tha</span>
  <span id="freeText11774429762595365146" style="display:none"><b>Thank you Edelweiss and HarperCollins for providing me with an ARC of this book!</b><br /><br /><b><u>Short review</u>:</b> <br /><br />I'm having a bit of difficulty expressing how I feel about this book. I really enjoyed it, and it had a lot of powerful moments. I appreciate that Neal Shusterman tackled a personal subject (from what I understand, his son struggles with mental illness––and actually did the illustrations in the book, which is cool).<br /><br />To be honest, though, this was not my favorite of his books. While I think it's great that he tried something new, I felt a little ... distant from the story and characters. I just didn't connect with it the same way I did with <i>Unwind</i>, the <i>Skinjacker</i> books, etc. But don't get me wrong––I just have ridiculously high expectations for Shusterman because I think he's one of the best YA authors out there.<br /><br />And this is still a great book. As much as I wish the characters had been a bit more well-developed, as a whole it's well-written, intriguing, and imaginative, and I think it will be important to a lot of people. <br /><br />------------<br /><br /><b>Full review coming eventually!</b></span>

<div id="review_1135322672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1135322672" />
    <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired"><img alt="Rashika (is tired)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476647072p2/8492956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1135322672?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rashika (is tired)" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired">Rashika (is tired)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=e-arcs">e-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=2015-favorites">2015-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=touchy-issues">touchy-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=mind-blown">mind-blown</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=realistic-contemporary">realistic-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=loved">loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=good-characters">good-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=awesomeness-redefined">awesomeness-redefined</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1135322672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17812698485683611439"><i>***This review has also been posted on <b><a href='http://wp.me/p3p0qg-1eI' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Social Potato</a></b></i><br/><br/>It would seem that 2015 is the year of all the fantastic books because here I am, finding yet another favorite. This book is gorgeously, frightengly written and it will find a way to creep inside your heart and hold it hostage.<strong> I make this book sound scary and believe me, it is.</strong><br/><br/>I don’t read a lot of books that deal with mental illness because admittedly, I am a chicken but this book called to me. I don’t know if it was the cover, or how the</span>
  <span id="freeText17812698485683611439" style="display:none"><i>***This review has also been posted on <b><a href="http://wp.me/p3p0qg-1eI" rel="nofollow noopener">The Social Potato</a></b></i><br /><br />It would seem that 2015 is the year of all the fantastic books because here I am, finding yet another favorite. This book is gorgeously, frightengly written and it will find a way to creep inside your heart and hold it hostage.<strong> I make this book sound scary and believe me, it is.</strong><br /><br />I don’t read a lot of books that deal with mental illness because admittedly, I am a chicken but this book called to me. I don’t know if it was the cover, or how the synopsis spoke of an adventure to the deep trenches (oh how I adore my adventures!). Whatever it was, I am glad that I decided to bite the bullet and read this, no matter how scared I was, because I would be missing out on a beautiful piece of work.<br /><br />I know there are many times I’ve said that I don’t know how I to start describing or book or put my feelings down on paper but I don’t think it’s been more true ever before. I keep trying to think of where I want to start talking about the actual book but I feel so insufficient,<strong> I don’t think anything I can say is enough for this beautiful gorgeous book and the sensitivity with which Neal dealt with something as delicate as mental illness.</strong><br /><br />Neal masterfully switches between two different timelines, the ‘real’ one and the ‘imaginary’ one. But really, what is real and imaginary? His use of second person in certain chapters was so gorgeous and almost moved me to tears. It really helped readers see Caden slowly spiraling out of control and it was heartbreaking.<br /><br />I couldn’t <em>not</em> talk about this book while reading it. I had to stop and read some pieces outloud to my friends just to have someone understand the emotional journey this book was taking me on and how terrifying it was!<br /><br /><strong>Neal makes Caden such a believable character and it’s impossible not to root for him.</strong> We see him muddled as a result of the drugs that he is given, we see him when the lines between reality and the imaginary start blurring and we see him coherent. I think what makes Caden so incredibly fantastic to read about is that even within all these various phases we see him in, nothing can strip him of what makes him, him. Which is what makes it all the more heartbreaking to see him in this muddled state where he floats in and out of reality, seeing things that aren’t there.<br /><br /><strong>What also makes Caden’s character so effective is that Neal never attempts to diagnose Caden</strong>, he mentions certain illness’ but he never really gives us a confirmed diagnosis, so those of us who are curious cats can rest in peace and continue to enjoy the story but still don't necessarily know what is going on with Caden. I don’t think it’s important to know Caden's diagnosis though. Neal does a fantastic job of showing you what is going on with Caden that giving a name to what is happening to him wouldn’t really change anything.<br /><br />Neal so fantastically develops the secondary characters as well and what made me especially happy was that <strong>Caden’s parents weren't shown as the bad guys!</strong> Maybe they could have caught on earlier but it is clear that they only want what is best for their son. They don’t abandon him to deal with this illness on his own. They are there, trying to help him even if they aren’t sure what is the best way of dealing with the situation on hand.<br /><br />That said, the secondary characters are not a huge part of this novel. The book remains Caden’s story and nothing can change that.<br /><br /><strong>I also absolutely ADORED the parallels between the real and imaginary worlds and it really helped readers see how hard it was for Caden to cling to reality in those moments.</strong> We see things in the real world that we had only seen in the imaginary world before and things click. Through the imaginary world, we really get to see aspects of the situation we might not have in the real world and it broke my heart.<br /><br /><strong>I will admit that this book was a little confusing at the beginning</strong> but when the parallels made themselves more evident, I really started enjoying the book.  I don't think that everything is meant to make sense right away because we are being immersed within the mind of someone suffering from a mental illness. It's why I never saw my confusion as a bad thing.<br /><br /><strong>This is a skilfully written novel and one I will not be forgetting anytime soon.</strong> Neal knows exactly what he is doing. Caden’s journey is beautiful to read about and while I know that this is not a book for everyone, it is still one I would want more people to read because of how important it is. So, if you’re scared, don’t be, there is a good chance you’ll fall head over heels for this gorgeous book, just like I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17812698485683611439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061134111" href="/book/show/22864710-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22027176-connor?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1551230493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14091487279332506654">I have so many thoughts on this book that this will be my first video review of the year. I'll link it here when I make it and post it on my channel. So great!<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://youtu.be/AFn5VXD3Ouw'>http://youtu.be/AFn5VXD3Ouw</a></span>
  <span id="freeText14091487279332506654" style="display:none">I have so many thoughts on this book that this will be my first video review of the year. <div id="review_1736511996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1736511996" />
    <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga"><img alt="Beatrice Masaluñga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603719912p2/4590441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1736511996?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrice Masaluñga" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga">Beatrice Masaluñga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Beatrice by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/25959228-cw-the-quiet-pond">CW (The Quiet Pond) ✨</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1736511996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12960118044074412435"><i>Challenger Deep</i> is vivid and masterfully written. It's an eye opening book about mental health as our protagonist, <b>Caden Bosch</b>, a 15 year old boy who suffers from Schizophrenia. We get to see his long journey as he struggles from such illness and his road to recovery. At first, you might find it complicated because he's in some kind of adventure, on a ship with a Pirate, and Caden is one of the crewmen as they head towards Marianas Trench to find a place called Challenger Deep. You'll be thinkin</span>
  <span id="freeText12960118044074412435" style="display:none"><i>Challenger Deep</i> is vivid and masterfully written. It's an eye opening book about mental health as our protagonist, <b>Caden Bosch</b>, a 15 year old boy who suffers from Schizophrenia. We get to see his long journey as he struggles from such illness and his road to recovery. At first, you might find it complicated because he's in some kind of adventure, on a ship with a Pirate, and Caden is one of the crewmen as they head towards Marianas Trench to find a place called Challenger Deep. You'll be thinking there's something <i>deeper</i> behind this and as the story unfolds, you'll see the clearer picture of its true meaning. <br /><br /><b>Neal Shusterman accurately portrayed mental illness, specifically Schizophrenia.</b> He doesn't sugarcoat of what actually happens on a person suffering with mental illness. There are hallucinations, delusions, disorganized thoughts and other signs and symptoms, even it's treatments (medications, therapies etc.). I love this book because it's <b>realistic and not romanticized</b>. As quoted in the book: <i>"Nothing is inevitable"</i> -- Mental illness can be treated but it doesn't disappear. Relapse may happen but it can be prevented as long as the person practices a healthy lifestyle and proper intake of prescribed medications. <br /><br />Educating, understanding and raising an awareness can make a huge difference to those who suffered mental disorders. We shouldn't be scared or left them hanging instead, we should listen on their cries when they need help before they further destroy themselves. There's one quote in this book that left a huge impact:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Dead kids are put on pedestals but mentally ill kids get hidden under the rug.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I would like to thank <a href="https://readthinkponder.wordpress.com/2016/08/23/book-recs-youre-portraying-it-right-mental-illnesses-in-ya" rel="nofollow noopener">CW</a> for recommending this book to me [click her name to read her other other recommendations of positive portrayals of Mental Illnesses in YA and this book is one of them.]</span>
  <a data-text-id="12960118044074412435" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5100924478097697981">This book had more layers than I even know how to begin with. <br/><br/>I knew going in this would be a tough read, one that in theory reads quickly, but the subject matter is heavy and deserves time to process as the reader makes their way through the Marianas Trench and the brain of Caden Bosch (cool name, right?).<br/><br/>Caden is 15 and struggling with dual timelines, grasping school and the pressures of teenage life along with the alternate reality of assisting the captain on the ship as it ventures into part</span>
  <span id="freeText5100924478097697981" style="display:none">This book had more layers than I even know how to begin with. <br /><br />I knew going in this would be a tough read, one that in theory reads quickly, but the subject matter is heavy and deserves time to process as the reader makes their way through the Marianas Trench and the brain of Caden Bosch (cool name, right?).<br /><br />Caden is 15 and struggling with dual timelines, grasping school and the pressures of teenage life along with the alternate reality of assisting the captain on the ship as it ventures into parts unknown to get to the bottom of the Marianas Trench. Slowly these stories merge together and I'm going to leave it at that as I don't want to give anything away. Shusterman brilliantly reveals the connections and as a reader I could feel my jaw drop with each realization of what was unfolding and what was underneath throughout the entire novel. This is such a tough subject to write about and after reading the afternote I have even more respect for Shusterman as he worked to create this book.<br /><br />One I would encourage everyone to read.</span>

<div id="review_1416384022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1416384022" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1416384022?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061134111" href="/book/show/22864710-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1416384022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2279753496953570593">National Book Award Winner!! Congratulations, Neal!!<br/><br/>My experiment to read all NBA Finalists in Young People's Literature is complete! I have personally selected Challenger Deep as the winner. We'll see who wins on 11/18! Read about my experiment and all nominees <a href='http://www.fortheloveofwords.net/national-book-awards-2015-my-pick/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>.<br/><br/>My rating: 4.5 of 5 stars<br/><br/><b>
  <i>‘Sometimes the darkness beyond is not glorious at all, it truly is an absolute absence of light. A clawing, needy tar that pulls you down. You drown but you don’t. It turns you to lead so you sink faster </i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText2279753496953570593" style="display:none">National Book Award Winner!! Congratulations, Neal!!<br /><br />My experiment to read all NBA Finalists in Young People's Literature is complete! I have personally selected Challenger Deep as the winner. We'll see who wins on 11/18! Read about my experiment and all nominees <a href="http://www.fortheloveofwords.net/national-book-awards-2015-my-pick/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br />My rating: 4.5 of 5 stars<br /><br /><b>
  <i>‘Sometimes the darkness beyond is not glorious at all, it truly is an absolute absence of light. A clawing, needy tar that pulls you down. You drown but you don’t. It turns you to lead so you sink faster in its viscous embrace. It robs you of hope and even the memory of hope. It makes you think you’ve always felt like this, and there’s no place to go but down, where it slowly, ravenously digests your will, distilling it into the ebony crude of nightmares.’</i>
</b><br /><br />Caden Bosch’s descent into schizophrenia takes readers on an unforgettable adventure that blurs the line between what’s real and what’s mere fantasy. Caden is a gifted artist at the age of fifteen years old yet he possesses an inner drive, a compulsion, that he can no longer keep quiet. His art becomes frenetic and he begins walking his town for hours based on a uncontrollable desire to fill the empty sidewalks with his presence. And sometimes his mind takes him elsewhere, where he’s a part of a crew on a galleon and their mission is to reach the deepest point of the Marianas Trench, a place called Challenger Deep.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>‘The things I feel cannot be put into words, or if they can, the words are in no language anyone can understand. My emotions are talking in tongues.’</i>
</b><br /><br />Ironically, this was my first read in <a href="http://www.fortheloveofwords.net/national-book-awards-2015-picking-the-winner-experiment/" rel="nofollow noopener">my National Book Award experiment</a>, yet it’s the last one I sat down to review. This was such a staggering read for me that it really took me some time to fully process Caden’s story and how it made me feel. I suppose the expected response is sadness and pity, but it was so authentically told that it transformed this story into something truly substantial for me. Despite the fantasy world that Caden lived in, his struggle becomes something real. We glimpse just enough of the outside world to realize how much his loved ones are also impacted and how they struggle to understand his inner turmoil. How his parents plead with him to change his behavior when it’s well past the point of his ability, so he’s placed in a mental institution when they don’t know what else to do for him. Almost in defiance of such a melancholy story, is the subtle (yet effective) humor that is laced throughout.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“If you continue making progress,” one of the nurses told me earlier today, “I see no reason why you shouldn’t be going home in a couple of weeks.” Then she added, “But don’t quote me on that.” Noncommittal is rampant among the committed.</i>
</b><br /><br />Sprinkled throughout this story are various pieces of art which are <a href="http://shustermania.storenvy.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">original pieces from the authors son, Brendan Shusterman</a>. The story itself exists solely because of the experiences of Brendan who has personally struggled with mental illness, which makes sense as to why this story rang so true for me. Challenger Deep will certainly leave readers who haven’t suffered personally to gain more of an understanding and compassion for those that do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2279753496953570593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1230980315" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1230980315" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1230980315?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061134111" href="/book/show/22864710-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1230980315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10323881882630345092">This review appears on <a href='http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2015/07/29/challenger-deep-by-neal-schusterman-review-diving-into-schizophrenia/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews! <br/><br/>Challenger Deep is not an easy read. But schizophrenia is not an easily understood illness. The book outlines the delusions, anxiety and paranoia which a schizophrenia sufferer experiences, at their worst, and it serves as a confronting and elegant look into a feared and misunderstood mental illness. I’m a big fan of books that tackle mental illness sensitively and realistically, and Challenger Deep had an artistic flair and</span>
  <span id="freeText10323881882630345092" style="display:none">This review appears on <a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/2015/07/29/challenger-deep-by-neal-schusterman-review-diving-into-schizophrenia/" rel="nofollow noopener">Happy Indulgence</a>. Check it out for more reviews! <br /><br />Challenger Deep is not an easy read. But schizophrenia is not an easily understood illness. The book outlines the delusions, anxiety and paranoia which a schizophrenia sufferer experiences, at their worst, and it serves as a confronting and elegant look into a feared and misunderstood mental illness. I’m a big fan of books that tackle mental illness sensitively and realistically, and Challenger Deep had an artistic flair and beauty that hasn’t been replicated anywhere else.<br /><br />I’m not going to lie, it took me a while to get used to the book. There’s no dallying around, it launches straight into these deep, hard hitting and impactful thoughts separated into several sections. My first impression was that these thoughts seemed to be random and jumbled together, and I wasn’t ready for that. But it soon pulled me into Caden Bosch’s frenetic and thoughtful mind, which was a wondrous, confusing and imaginative place, jumping from the “White Space Kitchen” ie. the hospital, to his place on a ship heading to Challenger Deep, medication, other patients, his parents.<br /><br />Knowing what this book is about from the beginning, would probably ease the jump into the book. It’s rather hard to follow from the start, as it interchanges Caden’s imagination with reality. In Caden’s imagination, the adventure on a ship, interacting with the parrot and the villainous captain could be seen as a rather nonsensical adventure. But once I realised that what was happening in his real life transferred over to his imagination when he regressed into his mind, it became easier to follow for me.<br /><br />Neal Schusterman’s author note at the end gave me goosebumps. Having experienced a close friend and his own son being diagnosed with schizophrenia, there’s no one else who could have offered such an elegant, heartfelt, thoughtful and accurate description of a patient suffering from the mental illness. It’s a scary place for both the patient and their family which was captured rather accurately here.<br /><br />Most importantly, Challenger Deep raised something that’s often unknown about mental illness – it’s never cured, but you can recover from it. You can move on and live life in normalcy, as long as you leave the medication and the management to the professionals, with the support of your loved ones.<br /><br />There’s been many mental illness books, such as All the Bright Places which use romance as a recovery tool. But Challenger Deep takes a different tact, focusing on Caden’s recovery and strength within himself. How many YA/NA books have you read, where people only recover because of romance? This one is more realistic, empowering, raw and honestly, hard-hitting and emotional.<br /><br />Challenger Deep is a powerful, artful and thought provoking novel, about a much misunderstood mental illness. It will confuse you, amaze you, grip you with raw emotion and leave you with a lasting impression. Seeing Caden go through such disturbing depths from his illness is an emotionally exhausting journey, but one that is an incredibly beautiful one. I could read this book again and have a completely different experience; that’s how deep it is.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10323881882630345092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2406416585" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2406416585" />
    <a title="Naima ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34968895-naima"><img alt="Naima ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483767201p2/34968895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2406416585?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naima ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naima ✩" href="/user/show/34968895-naima">Naima ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061134111" href="/book/show/22864710-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34968895-naima?shelf=hauled-in-2018">hauled-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34968895-naima?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34968895-naima?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34968895-naima?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2406416585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14704930987368151110">So this was my first ever <b>Neal Shusterman</b> book and can I just say what a genius this man is. This book was brilliant. <br/><br/>It’s about mental illness; more specifically: schizophrenia. Let me begin by saying that I knew next to nothing about Schizophrenia before reading this. I mean, i’d heard the word in passing and I knew <i>of</i> it but not what it was <i>really</i> like. <br/><br/>But the moment I started reading this, it felt so personal and <b>REAL</b> and I could tell that the mental illness representation was AMAZING. I 10</span>
  <span id="freeText14704930987368151110" style="display:none">So this was my first ever <b>Neal Shusterman</b> book and can I just say what a genius this man is. This book was brilliant. <br /><br />It’s about mental illness; more specifically: schizophrenia. Let me begin by saying that I knew next to nothing about Schizophrenia before reading this. I mean, i’d heard the word in passing and I knew <i>of</i> it but not what it was <i>really</i> like. <br /><br />But the moment I started reading this, it felt so personal and <b>REAL</b> and I could tell that the mental illness representation was AMAZING. I 100% knew that Neal Shusterman had done his research and done it very <i>well</i>. Then I read the author’s note in the end: HE WAS WRITING FROM HIS OWN PERSONAL EXPERIENCE; his son’s to be more specific. And the mc in this book sketches and is into art so there are a few illustrations scattered here and there and they were actually his SON’S!!!! How amazing is that??? Like they were actual legit sketches from a mentally ill patient. It just made more sense as to why I was so connected with the story. <br /><br />So in the beginning, it was kinda confusing. Half of the chapters are imaginary; what’s going on inside Caden’s mind. And half are real. The imaginary parts take place on a pirate’s ship so naturally it took me a while to understand what was actually happening. But godddd. I’ve heard so much about mental illness that I thought I actually understood it. But after reading this I have realized that I was <i>CLUELESS</i>. The paranoia, the delusions, the depression, it was so <i>much</i> and only reading about it made my head spin. I CAN’T IMAGINE WHAT IT WOULD REALLY BE LIKE, to have those thoughts all the time!! I was affected. <i>So affected</i>. <br /><br />This book taught me so much. <br /><br />-<b>First:</b> Mental illness can never have a correct diagnoses. You have to be on a trial with so many drugs and pills, to see which one works best for <b>you</b>. Because unlike other diseases, there isn’t one pill that will work the same with everyone. <br /><br />-<b>Second:</b> Mental illness can also never be cured. It can be controlled but never cured. <br /><br />To be honest, I wasn’t really fond of the imaginary parts of the book and found them kind of boring but they had their own <b>appeal</b> and were necessary to really understand what it’s like. And it was so interesting to see how, as the book was nearing it’s end and Caden was making progress with his treatment, the imaginary and real had started to interconnect and relate to each other. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to everyone who ever wants to know about mental illness or ANYONE IN GENERAL <b>because this needs more awareness</b>. Why isn’t this book more popular??? More people need to read it. Go read it!!!<br /><br />P.s did I mention I love this book cover?? It’s GORGEOUS. It’s my favourite shade of blue and I love ittt</span>
  <a data-text-id="14704930987368151110" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2268908899" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2268908899" />
    <a title="Hallie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42328851-hallie"><img alt="Hallie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429512183p2/42328851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2268908899?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hallie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hallie" href="/user/show/42328851-hallie">Hallie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062413093" href="/book/show/24331542-challenger-deep">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Hallie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/59737007-alia-you-are-not-your-anxiety">Alia ~you are not your anxiety~</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42328851-hallie?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42328851-hallie?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42328851-hallie?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42328851-hallie?shelf=need-to-read-again">need-to-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42328851-hallie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2268908899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7426660286202796827"><b>
  <i>“Dead kids are put on pedestals, but mentally ill kids get hidden under the rug.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I've been running around looking for good fiction books about suicide and depression for a while, and I was more than pleased when a great friend recommended this one. She seemed to like it a lot and it was her confidence that I would like it too that made me want to read this more than anything. And I'm glad that I did because <b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18075234.Challenger_Deep' title='Challenger Deep by Neal Shusterman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Challenger Deep</a> is the perfect book that portrays a mental illness.</b> I owe my friend a</span>
  <span id="freeText7426660286202796827" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Dead kids are put on pedestals, but mentally ill kids get hidden under the rug.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I've been running around looking for good fiction books about suicide and depression for a while, and I was more than pleased when a great friend recommended this one. She seemed to like it a lot and it was her confidence that I would like it too that made me want to read this more than anything. And I'm glad that I did because <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18075234.Challenger_Deep" title="Challenger Deep by Neal Shusterman" rel="nofollow noopener">Challenger Deep</a> is the perfect book that portrays a mental illness.</b> I owe my friend a lot for this.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“The scariest thing of all is never knowing what you're suddenly going to believe.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The story follows Caden Bosch, a fifteen year old boy, through series of hallucinations. As a result of schizoaffective disorder, Caden's world shifts between two parallel lives - one in which he is Caden Bosch, a high schooler and another in which he is on a ship headed for Challenger Deep, the earth's deepest point. It is an <b>extraordinary and compelling tale that portrays good illness perfectly.</b> It is well-written, sensitive and frightening, but yet gives a light sense of hope. It doesn't glamorize or romanticize mental disorders, and I believe, has an accurate portrayal, too.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“And when the abyss looks into you - and it will - may you look back unflinching.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Caden is a brilliant high school student, and his behavioral changes strike odd to his friends and family. His delusions that he is on a ship is very well-written and the change from imaginary to real life flows well. He and all the other characters seem so real that I could see Caden standing right before me. It was so <b>easy to connect with the characters.</b> And bonus points to his family, who were there for him through his struggles and their care is blatant. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“You see demons in the eyes of the world, and the world sees a bottomless pit in yours.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The writing style was absolutely immaculate. No flowery metaphors, no cheesy dialogues, nothing cliche and <b>was the perfect voice for a character with a mental disorder.</b> As I analysed this book meticulously, I noticed that there were 161 chapters but all in 304 pages. Each chapter wasn't too long to make the delusion seem - well, too delusional. The transition from delusion to real is smooth, and it's pretty easy to get that picture in my mind. It's beautiful. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“You see demons in the eyes of the world, and the world sees a bottomless pit in yours.” </i>
</b><br /><br />Candidly, in spite of all the excitement, I was a bit sceptical when I read the first two chapters. I had lost hope, but soon the story picked up and everything made sense. It was not meant to be purely a story for enjoyment. It was meant to be intangible and dramatic. <b>It was meant to be impeccable yet fallible.</b> It isn't a story to say 'Hey, so some people have mental disorders...' It has a serious tone, and is more than just a book for some light reading before bed. It is horrific, but beautiful.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“They all think medicine should be magic, and they become mad at me when it's not.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I can't praise this book enough! It is literally flawless! It's scary and terrifying, but still brings up hope. Moreover, the author does not glamorize Caden's situation, nor does he water it down. He portrays it as it is - painful and horrifying - and does not exaggerate the seriousness. It definitely isn't something I would normally enjoy since it is half imaginary and half real, I thought it was amazing. <b>It is indeed marvellous.</b> Subtle and serious and truly emotional. I believed that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17661416.Made_You_Up" title="Made You Up by Francesca Zappia" rel="nofollow noopener">Made You Up</a> would be the last book on this that I would love this much, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18075234.Challenger_Deep" title="Challenger Deep by Neal Shusterman" rel="nofollow noopener">Challenger Deep</a> is better. No, it's the best.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“It's a curse to see all that might happen but never know what will.”</i>
</b><br /><br />I'm sorry but this book just blew my mind away. It's so good I don't even know where to start. I can't emphasize the beauty in it, and it's all just beggars description. <b>I would definitely recommend it to <i>everyone</i>.</b> It is an intriguing page-turner, and even if you don't love it, it will still make you think about the message.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7426660286202796827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hkA9WLCS+ey1F/bF5EcsIPYw3GdJebVLIP8gIIucP4F7loVlbTOGZVp9NhZDC4xHZG02p+mazfDE+bcxqYOZGA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lSYEEjbjC5zIgcoJGRcjMT1N0I2J4pvrNkVRBqj+1K1o8Lwv60J0FSfrCtq+W4NWrxA6TSkB41DSQ8YXiuFyNA==')})
  }

See, his brother Shawn was just murdered. And Will knows the rules. No crying. No snitching. Revenge. That’s where Will’s now heading, with that gun shoved in the back waistband of his jeans, the gun that was his brother’s gun. He gets on the elevator, seventh floor, stoked. He knows who he’s after. Or does he? As the elevator stops on the sixth floor, on comes Buck. Buck, Will finds out, is who gave Shawn the gun before Will took the gun. Buck tells Will to check that the gun is even loaded. BUCK IS DEAD. But Buck’s in the elevator? Just as Will’s trying to think this through, the door to the next floor opens. A teenage girl gets on, waves away the smoke from Dead Buck’s cigarette. Will doesn’t know her, but she knew him. Knew. When they were eight. And stray bullets had cut through the playground, and Will had tried to cover her, but she was hit anyway, and so what she wants to know, on that fifth floor elevator stop, is, what if Will, Will with the gun shoved in the back waistband of his jeans, MISSES.And so it goes, the whole long way down, as the elevator stops on each floor, and at each stop someone connected to his brother gets on to give Will a piece to a bigger story than the one he thinks he knows. A story that might never know an END…if WILL gets off that elevator.Told in short, fierce staccato narrative verse, Long Way Down is a fast and furious, dazzlingly brilliant look at teenage gun Then you have more in common than you know with lonely homesteaders in 18th century New England. At once heartwarming and heartbreaking, Matrimony, Inc. reveals the unifying thread that weaves its way through not just marriage and relationships over the centuries, but American social history itself: advertising for  love.  Amazingly, America’s first personal ad appeared in the Boston Evening Post as early as 1759. A “person who flatters himself that he shall not be thought disagreeable” was in search of a “young lady, between the age of eighteen and twenty-three, of a middling stature, brown hair, of good Morals…” As family-arranged marriages fell out of fashion, &quot;Husband Wanted&quot; or &quot;Seeking Wife&quot; ads were soon to be found in every state in the nation.  From the woman in a Wisconsin newspaper who wanted “no brainless dandy or foppish fool” to the man with a glass eye who placed an ad in the New York Times hoping to meet a woman with a glass eye, the many hundreds of personal ads that author Francesca Beauman has uncovered offer an extraordinary glimpse into the history of our hearts’ desires, as well as a unique insight into American life as the frontier was settled and the cities grew. Personal ads played a surprisingly vital role in the West: couple by couple, shy smile by shy smile, letter by letter from a dusty, exhausted miner in California to a bored, frustrated seamstress in Ohio. Get ready for a new perspective on the making of modern America, a hundred words of typesetter’s blurry black ink at a time.  “So anxious are our settlers for wives that they never ask a single lady her age. All they require is teeth,” declared the Dubuque Iowa News in 1838 in a state where men outnumbered women three to one. While the dating pools of 21st century New York, Chicago or San Francisco might not be quite so dentally-fixated, Matrimony Inc. will put idly swiping right on Tinder into fascinating and vividly fresh historical context. What do women look for in a man? What do men look for in a woman? And how has this changed over the past 250 years?<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"8908888852792998196\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/19564.Neal_Shusterman">About Neal Shusterman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/19564.Neal_Shusterman"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1246977170p3/19564.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/19564.Neal_Shusterman">Neal Shusterman
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
18,559
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15830957560650862666">Award-winning author Neal Shusterman grew up in Brooklyn, New York, where he began writing at an early age. After spending his junior and senior years of high school at the American School of Mexico City, Neal went on to UC Irvine, where he made his mark on the UCI swim team, and wrote a successful humor column. Within a year of graduating, he had his first book deal, and was hired to write a movi</span>
  <span id="freeText15830957560650862666" style="display:none">Award-winning author Neal Shusterman grew up in Brooklyn, New York, where he began writing at an early age. After spending his junior and senior years of high school at the American School of Mexico City, Neal went on to UC Irvine, where he made his mark on the UCI swim team, and wrote a successful humor column. Within a year of graduating, he had his first book deal, and was hired to write a movie script.<br /><br />In the years since, Neal has made his mark as a successful novelist, screenwriter, and television writer. As a full-time writer, he claims to be his own hardest task-master, always at work creating new stories to tell. His books have received many awards from organizations such as the International Reading Association, and the American Library Association, as well as garnering a myriad of state and local awards across the country. Neal's talents range from film directing (two short films he directed won him the coveted CINE Golden Eagle Awards) to writing music and stage plays – including book and lyrical contributions to “American Twistory,” which is currently playing in Boston. He has even tried his hand at creating Games, having developed three successful "How to Host a Mystery" game for teens, as well as seven "How to Host a Murder" games.<br /><br />As a screen and TV writer, Neal has written for the "Goosebumps" and “Animorphs” TV series, and wrote the Disney Channel Original Movie “Pixel Perfect”. Currently Neal is adapting his novel Everlost as a feature film for Universal Studios.<br /><br />Wherever Neal goes, he quickly earns a reputation as a storyteller and dynamic speaker. Much of his fiction is traceable back to stories he tells to large audiences of children and teenagers -- such as his novel The Eyes of Kid Midas. As a speaker, Neal is in constant demand at schools and conferences. Degrees in both psychology and drama give Neal a unique approach to writing. Neal's novels always deal with topics that appeal to adults as well as teens, weaving true-to-life characters into sensitive and riveting issues, and binding it all together with a unique and entertaining sense of humor.<br /><br />Of Everlost, School Library Journal wrote: “Shusterman has reimagined what happens after death and questions power and the meaning of charity. While all this is going on, he has also managed to write a rip-roaring adventure…”<br /><br />Of What Daddy Did, Voice of Youth Advocates wrote; "This is a compelling, spell-binding story... A stunning novel, impossible to put down once begun.<br /><br />Of The Schwa Was Here, School Library Journal wrote: “Shusterman's characters–reminiscent of those crafted by E. L. Konigsburg and Jerry Spinelli–are infused with the kind of controlled, precocious improbability that magically vivifies the finest children's classics.<br /><br />Of Scorpion Shards, Publisher's Weekly wrote: "Shusterman takes an outlandish comic-book concept, and, through the sheer audacity and breadth of his imagination makes it stunningly believable. A spellbinder."<br /><br />And of The Eyes of Kid Midas, The Midwest Book Review wrote "This wins our vote as one of the best young-adult titles of the year" and was called "Inspired and hypnotically readable" by School Library Journal.<br /><br />Neal Shusterman lives in Southern California with his children Brendan, Jarrod, Joelle, and Erin, who are a constant source of inspiration!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15830957560650862666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
